Taliban commander and governor Mullah Niazi banned prayer at Shia mosques<sup id="cite_ref-258"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-258">[256]</a></sup> and expressed [takfir](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Takfir "Takfir") of the Shia in a declaration from Mazar's central mosque:

> Last year you rebelled against us and killed us. From all your homes you shot at us. Now we are here to deal with you. The [Hazaras](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hazara_people "Hazara people") are not Muslims and now we have to kill Hazaras. You must either accept to be Muslims or leave Afghanistan. Wherever you go, we will catch you. If you go up we will pull you down by your feet; if you hide below, we will pull you up by your hair.<sup id="cite_ref-259"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-259">[257]</a></sup>

Assisting the Taliban in the murder of Iranian diplomatic and intelligence officials at the Iranian Consulate in Mazar were "several Pakistani militants of the anti-Shia, Sipah-e-Sahaba party."<sup id="cite_ref-260"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-260">[258]</a></sup> There were other pogroms of Shia as well in the first Taliban reign prior to the U.S. invasion.<sup id="cite_ref-261"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-261">[259]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-262"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-262">[260]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-263"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-263">[261]</a></sup>

In 2021 [Human Rights Watch](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch "Human Rights Watch") warned on a "surge in Islamic State Attacks on Shia" in Afghanistan "that amount to crimes against humanity".<sup id="cite_ref-HRW-2021-Afghanistan_264-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-HRW-2021-Afghanistan-264">[262]</a></sup> Attacks on the Hazara Shia community include

-   suicide bombings that killed at least 72 people at the Sayed Abad mosque in Kunduz on October 8, 2021,<sup id="cite_ref-HRW-2021-Afghanistan_264-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-HRW-2021-Afghanistan-264">[262]</a></sup>
-   a bombing that killed at least 63 people at the Bibi Fatima mosque in Kandahar on October 15, 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-HRW-2021-Afghanistan_264-2"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-HRW-2021-Afghanistan-264">[262]</a></sup>

In a statement ISIS declared it would target Shia

> “in every way, from slaughtering their necks to scattering their limbs… and the news of \[ISIS’s\] attacks…in the temples of the \[Shia\] and their gatherings is not hidden from anyone, from Baghdad to Khorasan.”<sup id="cite_ref-HRW-2021-Afghanistan_264-3"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-HRW-2021-Afghanistan-264">[262]</a></sup>

### Nigeria [edit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations&action=edit&section=55 "Edit section: Nigeria")

In Nigeria—the most populous country in Africa—until recently almost all Muslims were Sunni.<sup id="cite_ref-265"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-265">[263]</a></sup> As of 2017, estimates of the number of Nigeria's 90–95 million Muslims who are Shia vary from between 20 million (Shia estimate), to less than five million (Sunni estimate)<sup id="cite_ref-:0_266-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-:0-266">[264]</a></sup> but according to [Pew research center](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pew_research_center "Pew research center"), less than 5% of the Muslim population in Nigeria are Shia.<sup id="cite_ref-Pew2009Web_14-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-Pew2009Web-14">[14]</a></sup>

In the 1980s, [Ibrahim El-Zakzaky](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ibrahim_Zakzaky "Ibrahim Zakzaky")—a Nigerian admirer of the [Iranian Revolution](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iranian_Revolution "Iranian Revolution") who lived in Iran for some years and converted to Shia Islam—established the [Islamic Movement of Nigeria](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_Movement_(Nigeria) "Islamic Movement (Nigeria)"). The movement has established "more than 300 schools, Islamic centers, a newspaper, guards and a \`martyrs’ foundation\`".<sup id="cite_ref-:0_266-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-:0-266">[264]</a></sup> Its network is similar to that of [Hezbollah](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hezbollah "Hezbollah") in Lebanon, with a focus on Iran, its [Supreme Leader](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supreme_Leader_of_Iran "Supreme Leader of Iran"), and fighting America as the enemy of Islam.<sup id="cite_ref-267"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-267">[265]</a></sup> According to a former U.S. State Department specialist on Nigeria, Matthew Page, the Islamic Movement receives "about $10,000 a month" in Iranian funding.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_266-2"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-:0-266">[264]</a></sup> Many of the converted are poor Muslims.

The Shia campaign has clashed with Saudi Arabian, which also funds religious centers, school, and trains students and clerics, but as part of an effort to spread its competing [Wahabbi](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_propagation_of_Salafism_and_Wahhabism "International propagation of Salafism and Wahhabism") interpretation of Islam.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_266-3"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-:0-266">[264]</a></sup> According to Wikileaks, "Saudi cables" released in 2015 "reveal concern" about "Iran-driven Shiite expansion from Mali, Mauritania, Burkina Faso and Nigeria" to Shia Islam has taken place in Nigeria since the Iranian Revolution.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_266-4"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-:0-266">[264]</a></sup>

Shia Muslims protest that they have been persecuted by the Nigerian government.<sup id="cite_ref-268"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-268">[266]</a></sup> In 1998 Nigerian President General [Sani Abacha](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sani_Abacha "Sani Abacha") accused Ibrahim El-Zakzaky <sup id="cite_ref-269"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-269">[267]</a></sup> of being a Shia. In December 2015 the Nigerian government alleged that the Islamic Movement attempted to kill Nigeria's army chief-of-staff. In retaliation, troops [killed more than 300](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/2015_Zaria_massacre "2015 Zaria massacre") Shiites in the city of [Zaria](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zaria "Zaria"). Hundreds of El-Zakzaky's followers were also arrested.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_266-5"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-:0-266">[264]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-270"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-270">[268]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-271"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-271">[269]</a></sup> As of 2019, El-Zakzaky was still imprisoned.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_266-6"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-:0-266">[264]</a></sup>

### South East Asia [edit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations&action=edit&section=56 "Edit section: South East Asia")

Islam is the dominant religion in [Indonesia](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indonesia "Indonesia"), which also has a larger Muslim population than any other country in the world, with approximately 202.9 million identified as Muslim (88.2% of the total population) as of 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-Pew2009Web_14-2"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-Pew2009Web-14">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mgmpPRC_272-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-mgmpPRC-272">[270]</a></sup>

The majority adheres to the [Sunni](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sunni "Sunni") Muslim tradition mainly of the [Shafi'i](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shafi%27i "Shafi'i") [madhhab](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Madhhab "Madhhab").<sup id="cite_ref-273"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-273">[271]</a></sup> Around one million are [Shias](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia "Shia"), who are concentrated around [Jakarta](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jakarta "Jakarta").<sup id="cite_ref-imamreza_274-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-imamreza-274">[272]</a></sup> In general, the Muslim community can be categorized in terms of two orientations: "modernists," who closely adhere to orthodox theology while embracing modern learning; and "traditionalists," who tend to follow the interpretations of local religious leaders (predominantly in [Java](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Java "Java")) and religious teachers at Islamic boarding schools ([pesantren](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pesantren "Pesantren")). In Indonesia, in 2015, Sunni clerics denounced the Shia as "heretics", and the mayor of [Bogor](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bogor "Bogor") proposed banning the Shia [Ashura](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Day_of_Ashura "Day of Ashura") holy day.<sup id="cite_ref-275"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-275">[273]</a></sup> The Shia community (which makes up approximately 1% of Indonesia's Muslims) has also been subject to hate campaigns and intimidation, with fears of this escalating into violence.<sup id="cite_ref-276"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-276">[274]</a></sup>

[Malaysia](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Religion_in_Malaysia "Religion in Malaysia") claims to be a tolerant Islamic state, however since 2010 it has banned the preaching of Shia Islam, with a "particular ferocity"<sup id="cite_ref-economist_277-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-economist-277">[275]</a></sup> and warns against Shiism with its, "evil and blasphemous beliefs".<sup id="cite_ref-278"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-278">[276]</a></sup>

### United States [edit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations&action=edit&section=57 "Edit section: United States")

In late 2006 or early 2007, in what journalist [Seymour Hersh](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Seymour_Hersh "Seymour Hersh") called _The Redirection_, the United States changed its policy in the Muslim world, shifting its support from the Shia to the Sunni, with the goal of "containing" Iran and as a by-product bolstering Sunni extremist groups.<sup id="cite_ref-279"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-279">[277]</a></sup> Richard Engel, who is an NBC News Chief Foreign Correspondent, wrote an article in late 2011 alleging that the United States Government is pro-Sunni and anti-Shia. During the [Iraq War](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iraq_War "Iraq War"), the United States feared that a Shiite-led, Iran-friendly Iraq could have major consequences for American national security. However, nothing can be done about this as Iraq's Shiite government were democratically elected.<sup id="cite_ref-280"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-280">[278]</a></sup> Shadi Bushra of [Stanford University](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stanford_University "Stanford University") wrote that the United States’ support of the Sunni monarchy during the [Bahraini uprising](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bahraini_uprising_(2011%E2%80%93present) "Bahraini uprising (2011–present)") is the latest in a long history of US support to keep the Shiites in check. The United States fears that Shiite rule in the Persian Gulf will lead to anti-US and anti-Western sentiment as well as Iranian influence in the Arab majority states.<sup id="cite_ref-281"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-281">[279]</a></sup> One analyst told CNN that the US strategy on putting pressure on Iran by arming its Sunni neighbors is not a new strategy for the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-282"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-282">[280]</a></sup>

### Europe [edit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations&action=edit&section=58 "Edit section: Europe")

In Europe Shia-Sunni acrimony is part of life for tens of millions of European Muslims.<sup id="cite_ref-economist_277-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-economist-277">[275]</a></sup>

### Australia [edit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations&action=edit&section=59 "Edit section: Australia")

Conflict between religious groups in the [Middle East](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_East "Middle East") have spread to the Australian Muslim community<sup id="cite_ref-283"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-283">[281]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-284"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-284">[282]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-285"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-285">[283]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-286"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-286">[284]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-287"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-287">[285]</a></sup> and within Australian schools.<sup id="cite_ref-aussieteens_288-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-aussieteens-288">[286]</a></sup>

### ISIL and the 2013–2017 war in Iraq [edit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations&action=edit&section=60 "Edit section: ISIL and the 2013–2017 war in Iraq")

Growing out of the [2003 US invasion of Iraq](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/2003_invasion_of_Iraq "2003 invasion of Iraq") and overthrow of Iraqi government of [Saddam Hussein](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saddam_Hussein "Saddam Hussein"), a [Salafi jihadi](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Salafi_jihadism "Salafi jihadism") [extremist](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_extremism "Islamic extremism") militant group led by Sunni Arabs from Iraq and Syria,<sup id="cite_ref-289"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-289">[287]</a></sup> developed an insurgency that by March 2015 had control over territory in [Iraq](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iraq "Iraq") and [Syria](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Syria "Syria")<sup id="cite_ref-Pakistani_Taliban_pledges_allegiance_to_ISIL_290-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-Pakistani_Taliban_pledges_allegiance_to_ISIL-290">[288]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ISIL_gains_supporters_291-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-ISIL_gains_supporters-291">[289]</a></sup> occupied by ten million people.<sup id="cite_ref-292"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-292">[290]</a></sup> It proclaimed itself a worldwide [caliphate](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caliphate "Caliphate"),<sup id="cite_ref-293"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-293">[291]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-newname_294-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-newname-294">[292]</a></sup> with religious, political, and military authority over [Muslims worldwide](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ummah "Ummah").<sup id="cite_ref-What_does_ISIS'_declaration_of_a_caliphate_mean_295-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-What_does_ISIS'_declaration_of_a_caliphate_mean-295">[293]</a></sup> and dubbed itself _the_ Islamic State (الدولة الإسلامية, _ad-Dawlah al-Islāmiyah_),<sup id="cite_ref-BBCSep2014_296-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-BBCSep2014-296">[294]</a></sup> but by December 2017, it controlled just 2% of the territory it had at the peak of its expansion,<sup id="cite_ref-297"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-297">[295]</a></sup> and had been driven underground in Iraq.<sup id="cite_ref-298"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-298">[296]</a></sup>

In the few years of its success, it was responsible for human rights abuses and [war crimes](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/War_crime "War crime") (United Nations), and [ethnic cleansing](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ethnic_cleansing "Ethnic cleansing") on a "historic scale" ([Amnesty International](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amnesty_International "Amnesty International")), particularly of Shia Muslims. According to [Shia rights watch](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia_rights_watch "Shia rights watch"), in 2014 ISIS forces killed over 1,700 Shia civilians at Camp Speicher in [Tikrit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tikrit "Tikrit") Iraq, and 670 Shia prisoners at the detention facility on the outskirts of [Mosul](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mosul "Mosul").<sup id="cite_ref-ICAH_299-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-ICAH-299">[297]</a></sup> In June 2014, after ISIS had "seized vast territories" in western and northern Iraq, there were "frequent accounts of fighters’ capturing groups of people and releasing the Sunnis while the Shiites are singled out for execution", according to the New York Times. ISIS used a list of questions to "tell whether a person is a Sunni or a Shiite"—What is your name? Where do you live? How do you pray? What kind of music do you listen to?<sup id="cite_ref-rubin-questions-nyt_300-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-rubin-questions-nyt-300">[298]</a></sup>

After the collapse of the Iraqi army and capture of the city of [Mosul](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mosul "Mosul") by ISIS in June 2014, the "most senior"<sup id="cite_ref-bbc-sistani_301-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-bbc-sistani-301">[299]</a></sup> Shia spiritual leader based in Iraq, the Grand Ayatollah [Ali al-Sistani](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ali_al-Sistani "Ali al-Sistani"), who had been known as "pacifist" in his attitudes, issued a fatwa calling for jihad against ISIS and its Sunni allies, which was seen by the Shia militias as a "de facto legalization of the militias’ advance".<sup id="cite_ref-NYRB-ItSRiI_302-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-NYRB-ItSRiI-302">[300]</a></sup> In Qatari another Shiite preacher, Nazar al-Qatari, "put on military fatigues to rally worshipers after evening prayers," calling on them to fight against “the slayers of Imams [Hasan](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hasan_ibn_Ali "Hasan ibn Ali") and [Hussein](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Husayn_ibn_Ali "Husayn ibn Ali")” (the second and third [Imams](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Imamah_(Shia_doctrine) "Imamah (Shia doctrine)") of Shia history) and for Iran's supreme leader Ayatollah [Ali Khamenei](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ali_Khamenei "Ali Khamenei").<sup id="cite_ref-NYRB-ItSRiI_302-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-NYRB-ItSRiI-302">[300]</a></sup>

Shia militias fighting ISIS have also been accused of atrocities. [Human Rights Watch](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch "Human Rights Watch") has accused government-backed Shia militias of kidnapping and killing scores of Sunni civilians in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-econ-unsavory_303-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-econ-unsavory-303">[301]</a></sup>

#### Reduced to terror campaigns [edit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations&action=edit&section=61 "Edit section: Reduced to terror campaigns")

By 2019, the group resorted increasingly to terror bombings and insurgency operations, using its scattered underground networks of [sleeper cells](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sleeper_Cell "Sleeper Cell") across regions in the Middle East and various offshoots and adherents.<sup id="cite_ref-304"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-304">[302]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-305"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-305">[303]</a></sup>

According to military.com, as of May 2023, the Islamic State's Khorasan Province, (ISIS-K), has become "the new boogeyman in the Middle East".<sup id="cite_ref-Lawrence-boogeyman-2023_306-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-Lawrence-boogeyman-2023-306">[304]</a></sup> CNN also writes that "new data" shows that at least in Afghanistan, the "threat from ISIS is growing".<sup id="cite_ref-Mackintosh-safe-CNN-2023_307-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-Mackintosh-safe-CNN-2023-307">[305]</a></sup> Although the Shia – in particular the ethnic [Hazaras](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hazara_people "Hazara people") – are just one of the targets of ISIS-K, (along with symbolic targets, foreigners, the ruling Taliban itself), they have been targeted, for example in September 2022, when an educational facility, in "a Shiite area" of the Afghan capital of Kabul, was suicide bombed, killing 53 teenage students and injuring 110.<sup id="cite_ref-FAIZI-2022_308-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-FAIZI-2022-308">[306]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-PBS-kabul-2022_309-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-PBS-kabul-2022-309">[307]</a></sup>

## Unity efforts [edit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations&action=edit&section=62 "Edit section: Unity efforts")

In a special interview broadcast on [Al Jazeera](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al_Jazeera_Media_Network "Al Jazeera Media Network") on 14 February 2007, former Iranian president and chairman of the [Expediency Discernment Council](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Expediency_Discernment_Council "Expediency Discernment Council") of Iran, Ayatollah [Akbar Hashemi Rafsanjani](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Akbar_Hashemi_Rafsanjani "Akbar Hashemi Rafsanjani") and highly influential Sunni scholar [Yusuf al-Qaradawi](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yusuf_al-Qaradawi "Yusuf al-Qaradawi"), "stressed the impermissibility of the fighting between the Sunnis and the Shi’is" and the need to "be aware of the conspiracies of the forces of [hegemony](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hegemony "Hegemony") and [Zionism](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zionism "Zionism") which aim to weaken \[Islam\] and tear it apart in Iraq."<sup id="cite_ref-mideastwire.com_110-2"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-mideastwire.com-110">[110]</a></sup>

Rafsanjani asked "more than once who started" the inter-Muslim killing in Iraq. Al-Qaradawi denied Rafsanjani's statement that he knew where "those arriving to Iraq to blow Shi’i shrines up are coming from."<sup id="cite_ref-mideastwire.com_110-3"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-mideastwire.com-110">[110]</a></sup>

### Saudi–Iran summit [edit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations&action=edit&section=63 "Edit section: Saudi–Iran summit")

In a milestone for the two countries' relations, on 3 March 2007 King Abdullah of Saudi Arabia and President Mahmoud Ahmadinejad held an extraordinary [summit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Summit_(meeting) "Summit (meeting)") meeting. They displayed mutual warmth with hugs and smiles for cameras and promised "a thaw in relations between the two regional powers but stopped short of agreeing on any concrete plans to tackle the escalating sectarian and political crises throughout the Middle East."<sup id="cite_ref-nytimes.com_310-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-nytimes.com-310">[308]</a></sup>

On his return to Tehran, Ahmadinejad declared that:

> Both Iran and Saudi Arabia are aware of the enemies' conspiracies. We decided to take measures to confront such plots. Hopefully, this will strengthen Muslim countries against oppressive pressure by the imperialist front.<sup id="cite_ref-nytimes.com_310-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-nytimes.com-310">[308]</a></sup>

Saudi officials had no comment about Ahmadinejad's statements, but the Saudi official government news agency did say:

> The two leaders affirmed that the greatest danger presently threatening the Islamic nation is the attempt to fuel the fire of strife between Sunni and Shiite Muslims, and that efforts must concentrate on countering these attempts and closing ranks.<sup id="cite_ref-311"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-311">[309]</a></sup>

Saudi Foreign Minister Prince [Saud bin Faisal bin Abdul-Aziz](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saud_bin_Faisal_bin_Abdul-Aziz "Saud bin Faisal bin Abdul-Aziz") said:

> The two parties have agreed to stop any attempt aimed at spreading sectarian strife in the region.<sup id="cite_ref-312"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-312">[310]</a></sup>

Effort to bring unity between Sunni and Shia Muslims had been attempted by [Allama Muhammad Taqi Qummi](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Allama_Muhammad_Taqi_Qummi&action=edit&redlink=1 "Allama Muhammad Taqi Qummi (page does not exist)").<sup id="cite_ref-Qummi_92-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-Qummi-92">[92]</a></sup>

### Scholarly opinions [edit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations&action=edit&section=64 "Edit section: Scholarly opinions")

#### Sunni [edit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations&action=edit&section=65 "Edit section: Sunni")

-   [Sheikh Mahmoud Shaltut](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mahmud_Shaltut "Mahmud Shaltut") (April 1893 – December 1963): In a Fatwa Sheikh Shaltut declared worship according to the doctrine of the Twelve Shia to be valid and recognized the Shiite as an Islamic School.<sup id="cite_ref-shaltoot_313-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-shaltoot-313">[311]</a></sup>
-   [Muhammad Sayyid Tantawy](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muhammad_Sayyid_Tantawy "Muhammad Sayyid Tantawy") (28 October 1928 – 10 March 2010): "I think that anyone who believes that there is no god but Allah and that Muhammad is his Messenger is definitely a Muslim. Therefore, we have been supporting, for a long time, through Al-Azhar, many calls for the reconciliation of Islamic schools of thought. Muslims should work on becoming united, and protecting themselves from denominational sectarian fragmentation. There are no Shiites and no Sunni. We are all Muslims. Regretfully; the passions and prejudices that some resort to, are the reason behind the fragmentation of the Islamic nation."<sup id="cite_ref-majalla_314-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-majalla-314">[312]</a></sup>
-   [Sheikh Mohammed al-Ghazali](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mohammed_al-Ghazali "Mohammed al-Ghazali") (1917–1996): "It is the duty of all Muslims to unite against enemies of Islam and their propaganda".<sup id="cite_ref-ghazali_315-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-ghazali-315">[313]</a></sup>
-   Sheikh Abd al-Majid Salim stated in a letter he sent to Ayatollah Borujerdi: "The first thing that becomes obligatory to scholars, Shia or Sunni, is removing dissension from the minds of Muslims."<sup id="cite_ref-alavi_316-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-alavi-316">[314]</a></sup>
-   Vasel Nasr, the Grand Mufti of [Egypt](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Egypt "Egypt") (Mufti from 1996-2002): "We ask Allah to create unity among Muslims and remove any enmity, disagreement and contention in the ancillaries of [Fiqh](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fiqh "Fiqh") between them."<sup id="cite_ref-broujerdi_317-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-broujerdi-317">[315]</a></sup>

#### Shiite [edit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations&action=edit&section=66 "Edit section: Shiite")

-   [Ayatollah Seyyed Hossein Borujerdi](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Seyyed_Hossein_Borujerdi "Seyyed Hossein Borujerdi") (March 1875 – March 1961) sent a letter to Sheikh Abd al-Majid Salim, the Grand [Mufti](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mufti "Mufti") of Sunnis and former Chancellor of [Al-Azhar University](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Azhar_University "Al-Azhar University") and wrote: "I ask Almighty Allah to change ignorance, separation and distribution among different Islamic Schools to each other, to the actual knowledge and kindness and solidarity."<sup id="cite_ref-etehad_318-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-etehad-318">[316]</a></sup>
-   [Ayatollah Ruhollah Khomeini](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ruhollah_Khomeini "Ruhollah Khomeini") (May 1900 – June 1989): "We are oneness with Sunni Muslims. We are their brothers" and "It is obligatory for all Muslims that maintain unity."<sup id="cite_ref-319"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-319">[317]</a></sup>
-   [Ayatollah Seyed Ali Khamenei](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ayatollah_Seyed_Ali_Khamenei "Ayatollah Seyed Ali Khamenei") (born April 1939) said in a [Fatwa](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fatwa "Fatwa") about creating dissension: "In addition to dissension is contrary to the [Qur'an](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Qur%27an "Qur'an") and [Sunnah](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sunnah "Sunnah"), this weakens Muslims. So, creating dissension is forbidden ([Haram](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Haram "Haram"))."<sup id="cite_ref-broujerdi_317-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-broujerdi-317">[315]</a></sup>
-   [Ayatollah Ali al-Sistani](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ayatollah_Ali_al-Sistani "Ayatollah Ali al-Sistani") (born August 1930), in answer to the question "is anyone who says [Shahadah](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shahadah "Shahadah"), prays and follow one of the Islamic Schools, a Muslim?", Sistani replied: "Every one who says Shahadah, acts as you describe and does not have enmity towards [Ahl al-Bayt](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ahl_al-Bayt "Ahl al-Bayt"), is Muslim."<sup id="cite_ref-broujerdi_317-2"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-broujerdi-317">[315]</a></sup>

## Notes [edit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations&action=edit&section=68 "Edit section: Notes")

1.  **[^](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_ref-116 "Jump up")** After 200 mostly Shia Iranians were killed during hajj by a stampede and Saudi gunfire [Ali Khamene’i](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ali_Khamenei "Ali Khamenei"), (then the president of Iran), proclaimed that “They are now propagandizing and claiming that this incident was a war between Shi‘ites and Sunnis. This is a lie! Of course there is a war; but a war between the American perception of Islam and true revolutionary Islam.”<sup id="cite_ref-115"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup>
2.  **[^](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_ref-126 "Jump up")** Writing in 2016, Max Fisher argues "Sunni-Shia sectarianism is indeed tearing apart the Middle East, but is largely driven by the very modern and very political rivalry between Iran and Saudi Arabia", whose "real roots" are not theological.<sup id="cite_ref-Fisher-2016_99-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_note-Fisher-2016-99">[99]</a></sup>

44.  ^ [Jump up to: <sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup>](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_ref-Nasr,_Vali_2006,_p.43_44-0) [<sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup>](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_ref-Nasr,_Vali_2006,_p.43_44-1) Nasr, Vali, _The Shia Revival_, Norton, 2006, p. 43
45.  **[^](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_ref-45 "Jump up")** Nawawi; translated by Maulana Waheed-uz-Zaman Knan. "Volume 2". _Sharh-e-Muslim_. p. 28. Imam Ahmed Auzai and Ibn-e-Manzar have said that it is up to the worshipper to perform the prayer in the way he wants. Imam Malik said that a worshipper may fold his hands and place them on his chest and he may pray with unfolded hands, and that is what the Malikis got accustomed with, he further said that hands should be unfolded in obligatory prayers and should be folded in Nafl prayers and Lais bin Sa'ad also said the same thing.
46.  **[^](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_ref-46 "Jump up")** Maulana Waheed-uz-Zaman Knan. "Volume 1". _Tafseer-al-Baari Sharh-e-SAahih Bukhari_. Karachi, Pakistan. p. 389. Ibn-e-Qasim has reported the unfolding of hands from Imam Malik, and that is what is practised by the Imamia sect (Shia).
47.  **[^](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_ref-47 "Jump up")** "Volume 2". _Nail-al-Awtar_. p. 203. There is no such proven tradition from Holy Prophet\*P.B.U.H in regard of folding hands, therefore it is up to the worshipper (whether he offers the prayers with either folded or unfolded hands).
48.  **[^](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_ref-48 "Jump up")** "Volume 3". _Nail al-Awtar_. Ibn-e-Sayd al-Naas narrated from Awzai that it is optional to fold or unfold arms in prayer
49.  **[^](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_ref-49 "Jump up")** Ahmed al-Duwaish. "Volume 6". _Fatawa al-Lajna al-Daema_. Saudi Arabia. If someone prays with unfolded arms, his prayer is valid, because putting the right hand on the left is neither part of prayer's pillars nor is a condition of prayer, nor it is wajib (obligatory).

168.  **[^](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia%E2%80%93Sunni_relations#cite_ref-IRIvKSA_170-0 "Jump up")** Nasr, Seyyed Vali Reza (2006). [_The Shia Revival: How Conflicts Within Islam Will Shape the Future_](https://archive.org/details/shiarevivalhowco00nasr). W.W. Norton and Company. pp. [150](https://archive.org/details/shiarevivalhowco00nasr/page/150)–51. [ISBN](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/ISBN_(identifier) "ISBN (identifier)") [9780393329681](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780393329681 "Special:BookSources/9780393329681"). It was Khomeini's direct challenge to Saudi Arabia that galvanized Sunni opposition to the Iranian revolution and the Shia awakening. Khomeini saw the Saudi monarchy as an American lackey, an unpopular and corrupt dictatorship that could be easily overthrown. ... More important, Khomeini underrated the degree and intensity of Sunni religious support for the Saudi regime ... on several occasions used the annual hajj to stage protests with the aim of fomenting trouble in the kingdom as well as spreading revolutionary messages among the faithful from around the world. On one such occasion, in July 1987, things got so out of hand that clashes between Iranian pilgrims and Saudi police left 402 dead.
